*bus, unsigned int val);\n707: /*\n708:  * Interface for HD codec\n709:  */\n710: \n711: /*\n712:  * CORB / RIRB interface\n713:  */\n714: static int azx_alloc_cmd_io(struct azx *chip)\n715: {\n716: \tint err;\n717: \n718: \t/* single page (at least 4096 bytes) must suffice for both ringbuffes */\n719: \terr = snd_dma_alloc_pages(SNDRV_DMA_TYPE_DEV,\n720: \t\t\t\t \tmark_pages_wc(chip, &chip->rb, true);\n727: \treturn 0;\n728: }\n729: \n730: static void azx_init_cmd_io(struct azx *chip)\n731: {\n732: \tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n733: \t/* CORB set up */\n734: \tchip->corb.addr = chip->rb.addr;\n735: \tchip->corb.buf = (u32 *)chip->rb.area;\n736: \tazx_writel(chip, CORBLBASE, (u32)chip->corb.addr);\n737: \tazx_writel(chip, CORBUBASE, upper_32_bits(chip->corb.addr));\n738: \n739: \t/* set the corb size to 256 entries (ULI requires explicitly) */\n740: \tazx_writeb(chip, CORBSIZE, 0x02);\n741: \t/* set the corb write pointer to 0 */\n742: \tazx_writew(chip, CORBWP, 0);\n743: \t/* reset the corb hw read pointer */\n744: \tazx_writew(chip, CORBRP, ICH6_CORBRP_RST);\n745: \t/* enable corb dma */\n746: \tazx_writeb(chip, CORBCTL, ICH6_CORBCTL_RUN);\n747: \n748: \t/* RIRB set up */\n749: \tchip->rirb.addr = chip->rb.addr + 2048;\n750: \tchip->rirb.buf = (u32 *)(chip->rb.area + 2048);\n751: \tchip->rirb.wp = chip->rirb.rp = 0;\n752: \tmemset(chip->rirb.cmds, 0, sizeof(chip->rirb.cmds));\n753: \tazx_writel(chip, RIRBLBASE, (u32)chip->rirb.addr);\n754: \tazx_writel(chip, RIRBUBASE, upper_32_bits(chip->rirb.addr));\n755: \n756: \t/* set the rirb size to 256 entries (ULI requires explicitly) */\n757: \tazx_writeb(chip, RIRBSIZE, 0x02);\n758: \t/* reset the rirb hw write pointer */\n759: \tazx_writew(chip, RIRBWP, ICH6_RIRBWP_RST);\n760: \t/* set N=1, get RIRB response interrupt for new entry */\n761: \tif (chip->driver_caps & AZX_DCAPS_CTX_WORKAROUND)\n762: \t\tazx_writew(chip, RINTCNT, 0xc0);\n763: \telse\n764: \t\tazx_writew(chip, RINTCNT, 1);\n765: \t/* enable rirb dma and response irq */\n766: \tazx_writeb(chip, RIRBCTL, ICH6_RBCTL_DMA_EN | ICH6_RBCTL_IRQ_EN);\n767: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n768: }\n769: \n770: static void azx_free_cmd_io(struct azx *chip)\n771: {\n772: \tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n773: \t/* disable ringbuffer DMAs */\n774: \tazx_writeb(chip, RIRBCTL, 0);\n775: \tazx_writeb(chip, CORBCTL, 0);\n776: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n777: }\n778: \n779: static unsigned int azx_command_addr(u32 cmd)\n780: {\n781: \tunsigned int addr = cmd >> 28;\n782: \n783: \tif (addr >= AZX_MAX_CODECS) {\n784: \t\tsnd_BUG();\n785: \t\taddr = 0;\n786: \t}\n787: \n788: \treturn addr;\n789: }\n790: \n791: static unsigned int azx_response_addr(u32 res)\n792: {\n793: \tunsigned int addr = res & 0xf;\n794: \n795: \tif (addr >= AZX_MAX_CODECS) {\n796: \t\tsnd_BUG();\n797: \t\taddr = 0;\n798: \t}\n799: \n800: \treturn addr;\n801: }\n802: \n803: /* send a command */\n804: static int azx_corb_send_cmd(struct hda_bus *bus, u32 val)\n805: {\n806: \tstruct azx *chip = bus->private_data;\n807: \tunsigned int addr = azx_command_addr(val);\n808: \tunsigned int wp;\n809: \n810: \tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n811: \n812: \t/* add command to corb */\n813: \twp = azx_readb(chip, CORBWP);\n814: \twp++;\n815: \twp %= ICH6_MAX_CORB_ENTRIES;\n816: \n817: \tchip->rirb.cmds[addr]++;\n818: \tchip->corb.buf[wp] = cpu_to_le32(val);\n819: \tazx_writel(chip, CORBWP, wp);\n820: \n821: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n822: \n823: \treturn 0;\n824: }\n825: \n826: #define ICH6_RIRB_EX_UNSOL_EV\t(1<<4)\n827: \n828: /* retrieve RIRB entry - called from interrupt handler */\n829: static void azx_update_rirb(struct azx *chip)\n830: {\n831: \tunsigned int rp, wp;\n832: \tunsigned int addr;\n833: \tu32 res, res_ex;\n834: \n835: \twp = azx_readb(chip, RIRBWP);\n836: \tif (wp == chip->rirb.wp)\n837: \t\treturn;\n838: \tchip->rirb.wp = wp;\n839: \n840: \twhile (chip->rirb.rp != wp) {\n841: \t\tchip->rirb.rp++;\n842: \t\tchip->rirb.rp %= ICH6_MAX_RIRB_ENTRIES;\n843: \n844: \t\trp = chip->rirb.rp << 1; /* an RIRB entry is 8-bytes */\n845: \t\tres_ex = le32_to_cpu(chip->rirb.buf[rp + 1]);\n846: \t\tres = le32_to_cpu(chip->rirb.buf[rp]);\n847: \t\taddr = \t\t\tchip->rirb.res[addr] = res;\n852: \t\t\tsmp_wmb();\n853: \t\t\tchip->rirb.cmds[addr]--;\n854: \t\t} else\n855: \t\t\tsnd_printk(KERN_ERR SFX \"spurious response %#x:%#x, \"\n856: \t\t\t\t azx_rirb_get_response(struct hda_bus *bus,\n864: \t\t\t\t\t  unsigned int addr)\n865: {\n866: \tstruct azx *chip = bus->private_data;\n867: \tunsigned long timeout;\n868: \tunsigned long || do_poll) {\n876: \t\t\tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n877: \t\t\tazx_update_rirb(chip);\n878: \t\t\tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n879: \t\t}\n880: \t\tif (!chip->rirb.cmds[addr]) {\n881: \tif (!chip->polling_mode) {\n909: \t\tsnd_printk(KERN_WARNING SFX \"azx_get_response timeout, \"\n910: \t\t\t   \"switching to polling mode: last cmd=0x%08x\\n\",\n911: \t\t\t   \"disabling MSI: last cmd=0x%08x\\n\",\n919: \t\t\t   chip->last_cmd[addr]);\n920: \t\tfree_irq(chip->irq, chip);\n921: \t\tchip->irq = -1;\n922: \t\tpci_disable_msi(chip->pci);\n923: \t\tchip->msi The command was\n964:  *       intended for the BIOS only, and may get confused with unsolicited\n965:  *       responses.  So, we shouldn't use it for normal operation from the\n966:  *       driver.\n967:  *       I left the codes, however, for debugging/testing purposes.\n968:  */\n969: \n970: /* receive a response */\n971: static int azx_single_wait_for_response(struct azx *chip, unsigned int addr)\n972: {\n973: \tint timeout = 50;\n974: \n975: \twhile (timeout--) {\n976: \t\t/* check IRV busy bit */\n977: azx_power_notify(struct hda_bus *bus, bool power_up);\n1062: #endif\n1063: \n1064: /* reset codec link */\n1065: static int azx_reset(struct azx *chip, int full_reset)\n1066: {\n1067: \tint Now I understand the bug:\n\nThe issue is:\n1. `azx_init_chip` has an early return check that prevents reinitialization if `chip->initialized` is already set\n2. During suspend, `azx_suspend` doesn't reset `chip->initialized` to 0\n3. When resume calls `azx_init_chip(chip, 1)`, it returns immediately because `chip->initialized` is still 1\n4. This means `azx_init_cmd_io()` is never called during resume, so the CORB/RIRB hardware is not reinitialized\n5. Without proper CORB/RIRB setup, the codec commands timeout\n\nThe fix should be to reset `chip->initialized = 0` during suspend, or to modify `azx_init_chip` to always reinitialize the command I/O when called from resume with `full_reset=1`.\n\nLooking at the code structure, the most logical fix is to reset `chip->initialized = 0` in the `azx_suspend` function before stopping the chip, or to check the `full_reset` parameter in `azx_init_chip` to override the early return.\n\nActually, looking more carefully:\n- In `azx_init_chip`, the check is `if (chip->initialized) return;`\n- But the function is called with `azx_init_chip(chip, 1)` which means `full_reset=1`\n- The `full_reset` parameter is used in `azx_reset(chip, full_reset)` at line 1215\n\nThe fix should probably be to reset `chip->initialized = 0` during suspend, OR to have `azx_init_chip` check the `full_reset` parameter and proceed even if `chip->initialized` is set when `full_reset=1`.\n\nLet me look for similar code in the git history to see what changed between 3.6.11 and {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01JWQv11qXB2paEvKfKAZeVv","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I have a clear picture of the bug. Let me trace through the code flow:\n\nDuring **suspend** (`azx_suspend`):\n1. PCM streams are suspended\n2. `snd_hda_suspend(chip->bus)` is called\n3. `azx_stop_chip(chip)` is called\n4. IRQ is freed\n5. MSI is disabled  \n6. **IMPORTANT**: `chip->initialized` is NOT reset to 0\n\nDuring **resume** (`azx_resume`):\n1. PCI device is re-enabled\n2. PCI state is restored\n3. MSI is re-enabled (if `chip->msi` was set before suspend)\n4. IRQ is acquired\n5. `azx_init_pci(chip)` is called\n6. `azx_init_chip(chip, 1)` is called - **BUT THIS RETURNS EARLY!**\n   - Because `chip->initialized` is still 1 (set during the initial boot)\n   - So `azx_init_cmd_io(chip)` is NEVER called\n   - The CORB/RIRB hardware registers are NEVER reinitialized\n7. `snd_hda_resume(chip->bus)` tries to communicate with the codec\n8. But the CORB/RIRB is not initialized, so codec commands time out\n\nThe root cause is that the `chip->initialized` flag is never reset to 0 during suspend, preventing proper reinitialization during resume.\n\nThe fix is to reset `chip->initialized = 0` in the `azx_suspend` function, or to modify `azx_init_chip` to always reinitialize when `full_reset=1`.\n\nLooking at the code patterns, the most straightforward fix would be to either:\n1. Add `chip->initialized = 0;` in `azx_suspend` before or after `azx_stop_chip(chip)`\n\n\n2. OR modify `azx_init_chip` to check `full_reset` parameter\n\nActually, looking at the code more carefully, I think the proper fix is to check the `full_reset` parameter in `azx_init_chip`. The function is designed to be called with `full_reset=1` when you want to force a full reinitialization. The current code structure is:\n\n```c\nstatic void azx_init_chip(struct azx *chip, int full_reset)\n{\n    if (chip->initialized)\n        return;\n    \n    /* reset controller */\n    azx_reset(chip, full_reset);\n```\n\nThe issue is that the early return doesn't account for the `full_reset` flag. When `full_reset=1`, the function should skip the initialized check and proceed with reinitializing the CORB/RIRB and other critical hardware components. This would ensure that resume operations properly reinitialize the codec communication path.\n\nThe most straightforward solution is to modify the early return condition to allow reinitialization when `full_reset=1` is passed, or alternatively reset the `chip->initialized` flag at the start when a full reset is requested.","signature":"Et4aCkYICxgCKkAiqOjmDoBAh6myZ0GTLz/vnD+sMPhnE3X5UsE7YEPuS7kXoqKN6tMEqEjmCXvXu63pb+wSo2Lc2nF1E3vtFzO8Egy0OBpKy3IVlL7TdKIaDOh2OmAGR0do8kqSOiIw5jO4gXszgrsc4DHhCjeONFHux8DB3GOZwWTfLOlExU83Qk81cYVCP0LEnYKvl8XYKsUZ3nFX7lhQbML27tHWkMyqzfpq385LY/UdRX5DipgvLvClTYwdiVR70fNpU9HVFjRftAmu9Xa+HwnUC+CA+ZIdJZL09fw2NUr/Bb5KAkjtsfeMbM8mcoH/a1miVJJAxLwXJqKl3PAXmRnL1Iddgymk8ezvkmrMYUr5pVXIYd37pw3VZrGSQ/twTTZ8BimIDWwbuUyoO9URPkRy70w+g6ZNSCd0jtLjr7FRt7wWBAoomCNoR1uds9UR4ww1Dh+LQahqYCUmHyk7vCisE+fbVnk4vXKZ5suCRHD+I5BoM4xTsXj6g4CHMDy9kNDz9A7RHkmxdWWZclu5qQotH04ZJwlPE2oLria4pLZYIQXkNfXr63TCGn5+tP0H7e2JxgUfMGQfCDiXGBdZsUt3eJWhD8OcVTD774PODgJUW+H8uFDldHvPOwQiq7C3ppzOOmPO3mdMe+ciPx/BZ2ogg61k8f8eCXXso1gR696ERbiaNxEFnieE0L4XNAav17egx0r8ESmGx9nQZZS7U6slPHjvfbxfQRbBM6kfkD7vW2ZzfQEhO4c9dwKMpQvaqMx+ur5EG8lGEAFfG9F2lMyyC5B5PtXbgnSBPuRbUtuTQ71riBW7MtL4yr+7BRAc0UAaN54g9zTTlrLDdriI+eht/S70ZF2MdkEZRYNFI1ASPDV31ZI6ZomVk+GF3moazZrYzXTpTeVw+8RmCvNd4Ahl0J5ryC+7MAY06ib808tEQRyr8AnmXwJHsRpN9j3/ISLLUepoudNZCVjmfTvp/uLlneTVHMuZQCyVwdy4G1kFUruuvolGrghObuDn6crTn3rYG32hu9iDpPEZ5GvDfFkZx6T85OaoaM1DpfI61nmnvCBNVyql2qusgWwNyq5eXEW8YUWEUDigtk+Hxmbza+V1nJP6oD9eqXyGx/FOBGC1VtuY6SHJGtCToog99QhKX0g4BY8uZp57TTFDQT9Vnv/wmOGANfxQPO6UYnl9jGwEUOKFbJ1+r7szpuyUjnJtOZnNSRr7lFKHHf7O4OdKZS4O9wsojmpwIVyKcDluK3BoXloKaOXG5q3I9K2qVgYpkqcQlXwBUlJBJyTVXHnGjF7eanWUA/0bcn5uS+v1HZhp/vXHPm6p6SkPczk+ZLyuyAcH+/L8aHZw54ydFpzPaOjMdb1OcYLLWiwMitPIoNL88aN3CyRKiJgYk7oFUabWR/UXw3O+/pD/BdVDOQkK8fNtnnAJQsyqO52vr0PM73V0oX12nadqtvlpifnEFNz4NVI3xCEnrUtyTUONwRJcls9sgL1/4FKT02XtBE4VdwkPQ/Ys60Fk4VkdOuMpOyEnUGNtBR+XjBWDOqioeIsptFxeWbyPSiteNyEQjijTeCr2zsy1H1UtoOaUf0hyR0yUECeB8qhhS84fjjrY5Jtnt0eRgZCFZuhkh5bIy/sHmsDt4aqNekO3v2zQXQbI3MhsKnHEhn6dwzGtxN3h9BgQLeZseB9u8yD6ejNUXieM76I0n7UJWIchFfSRbVzhWEdBYAACBgQ8iTn9qH1ZT9G56NBqhMLP2deEMlhpVZlNaF8kGQWAAG9TdrZe2Ohm+kZ98swuerP5kHDqhQYBQ6BMbdJqZxB2zHKmfQ9jMUZp7QBk4TrZsXnZtNsDJVCVwOOq+IXyJq/DJxDoxa+S2ZTjvFn65JnqnhyKZ8TP6wWBmZUtW5IfMcV3d/R+mXx2NDYe+WN/6mOeWQyd96XfyHCuH1xBqXmAxiHAgSJsa0OqBW8/B5K04Oq Looking at the resume code at line 2561:\n```c\nazx_init_chip(chip, 1);\n```\n\nAnd at line 1211 in azx_init_chip:\n```c\nif (chip->initialized)\n    return;\n```\n\nSo if `chip->initialized = 1` already, the initialization is skipped. The problem is that after suspend, `chip->initialized` gets set to 0, but on resume it might not be getting properly re-initialized if there's a race condition or if the flag isn't being reset correctly between cycles.\n\nLooking at the bug report more carefully - it works on fresh boot but fails after multiple suspend-resume cycles. This suggests the state management between suspend and resume is breaking down. Maybe `azx_stop_chip` isn't properly clearing the initialized flag, or `azx_init_chip` is returning early when it shouldn't be.\n\nThe key issue is that after resume, `snd_hda_resume` tries to communicate with the codec, but the CORB/RIRB command I/O isn't properly set up. In `azx_init_chip`, the CORB/RIRB initialization at lines 1222-1223 only happens if `!chip->single_cmd`, but this code path might be skipped due to an early return condition.\n\nIf `chip->initialized` is already set to 1 when `azx_init_chip` runs during resume, the function returns early at line 1211-1212 without reinitializing the command I/O. This would explain why codec commands timeout after resume—the CORB/RIRB registers weren't reset. The puzzle is why `chip->initialized` wouldn't be cleared by `azx_stop_chip` during suspend, unless there's a separate resume path or an issue with how `azx_acquire_irq` manages this state.","signature":"EswgCkYICxgCKkBncTvxAYJ+DE01WXQuMlvNFBmtu6S+ulP+u+U3DoEoItVWmPpoYAdg3sltdrFksxDYrxeploLnkYQWL0sRFBT+EgzuSCnqBQQsUA7ss1gaDH6MgzSEVrE1HjTUoCIwkr56DHr/LhL/qz6knhUnktJvI77drLGZCdQvKRhbKUmIKZkGmBOzY85CMEIXGWS0KrMff8QXwjWMSsLyo4Jf1guzgqXKCIz6PeuBjUvyHnrpouXdmzjg786GuNhwClU5xEkIbZYrCuSvkWaRcX68esium6HXSDMa3VkSiu4nKYR/b5fDSwkJrSownsYQEvyxxAH95aOriKsUwWJn0Pu5QVBnnkd/GSetvIse5b/LgkefvZQOd+3cMlSR9QdgVztXFlOJ+Jomp57W7+YxHFrHhMG62YqJVBr8XOAlfnMInZ2KM28AU3E4nHj9MHbuvJz82i6PWOy9iEcklOwojCIHgoKfkwBRb7G/qHxuy2YMXiaPcWstJLQkoFOvSiO9esc//RVj3HSNAj1/bOA+PEHxucxdMqBVrUOP3XiEDSvm10P1RWoKC0EbOO3EBNVKLqi3X4CZzpSk4vk4zdXgZj0lnB/LaPNj16F24fggQ6/8c6QSqp7dTAY24XkjGUMo/EyupH1MXTBsJMoBCCDgZEoKKngk1ObzEXJQHiYQ0evh0k5KjMeeSGQfjjtxuVlaJ03jQY09M2q+MldzuxGIFpt0d+jFbpcxiGiiihiwqvwSLC75F8KhoHovp7GacTVNEHDIugAYRDnYzJ3hM2YnnAuw/QRx8aDGwdHKmoE8Ii5UviBdNvTVMSHg9ERjHRY0NkrCwTWjCzFtO/76YAD6jSxzRifl1j++OV2u5r+ljX2x9Zivw57zSP8MbrAI6z7IFZ/y/4Sa9Hc5y0H8XieIAKAg6zzjDGZ6VcvbGjAqK1T3rOFYZqCIfWYpgB45qhcCct0GCF79jlWVPVy1qDcCo/G7XaIEsGEDhAgOQt3gDlFY4LBjZBDtNaqIbY5/Yy7K1UDBNWC1Hhi5yzBe2+lNUt0bFrpaXU1ySUln46pKbGWpL7Gf6+7rDC6w3jombcmlaiOdlJNFaG9wzanB/9YM0ZSwvxwBwdOC6WoPeMzyow0LCfIN7Ib3LR4nFDDJK+5wmmD439waAhFFixrx5MzLfFE4Ccw68lTVYUvSFG5n4m5iujTDxMQ5oy7LzS67ShMZ+cj/FNDfjqAHabUNHMT4Pi2pr/GEPLxbHRwI3pK3J65OwwAaQ922bjocSjU6jDb5JNwaA6QVjaymfQ0XHEPPq3e4iBFX3/zlpoyqh5IjDqSN86jI08sLcSgzZrYooW2GWOK7JGL1gce7eU63ynm0FgyAYOF2CG/dgFFV9zG/qU5aQJcDLUzFHiEHo1gnMCGisLxKZGgGPj9vDXQVM5F0R4fc3pTDY6qED8rL8W8D0j4NdcWsqKWUtYOqsTcHWUOKQsm7urCgRH97NSdoQ/UoVu7Ps18PhYj7yfUUheDsbzXyMzlVVrn5VpywRSNPwQjBaax0hIEnVLWmjE0yEGO8L05VmBP6QR2VlfY1H7i7/rKgsd06TGweTkJn4tXqA3+IQy5O7OkI29EsORpV9+oS9Wqb0WIskM890eMFkewogj9xXZNgxt9QCojKeHT/YMCt3ySd3st5EjwMcojeV/hgBkgcWdNqEd4zT08mxj0ljSKz2ItozGHeIHrAcdHyaM34ThnpJ0w4KnwFyn/TdstveQgXnUQQGfKMjbS/VU6dh9rAykk/SXUytDo3m9Stf26mMXW5JTdlwOcNSfuih3UXeKMkOgtTFF+ZI2Mc3Drw/QxF+IOEWCA76Fa9EDZCY/So8IpthYw4honIDibztLBYmmMfmwySRTyNtYnipIzEGSaWq6jbsEHeQutX+y5LOp4s4BWZp/Ju6sWegsj2GmGFi6ncifbge7ojYas6He0mEL1UrONdChM I need to understand the exact sequence and why the problem happens after a few suspends, not after the first one.\n\nLet me re-examine the problem. The bug report says:\n- \"After a few suspends to ram (it doesn't necessarily happen after just one)\"\n- \"I see these messages in the kernel log right after resume\"\n\nSo the problem appears AFTER resume. The error messages are:\n- \"hda-intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to polling mode\"\n- \"hda-intel: No response from codec, disabling MSI\"\n- \"hda_intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to single_cmd mode\"\n\nThese are generated in the `azx_rirb_get_response` function.\n\nThe issue is that the CORB/RIRB is not properly reinitialized after resume, so when the codec tries to respond, the response system is broken.\n\nLet me think about the state after the first suspend-resume:\n1. Before suspend: `chip->initialized = 1`, `chip->polling_mode = 0`, `chip->single_cmd = 0`\n2. During suspend: `azx_stop_chip(chip)` sets `chip->initialized = 0`\n3. During resume: `azx_init_chip(chip, 1)` should reinitialize everything and set `chip->initialized = 1`\n\nIf everything works correctly, after the first resume, the chip should be reinitialized and working fine. But if the CORB/RIRB isn't properly reinitialized on subsequent resumes, polling mode won't help and the response system remains broken. The real issue might be in how `azx_resume` orders its operations—perhaps the IRQ is being acquired before the chip is fully reinitialized.\n\nLooking at the initialization sequence, `azx_init_pci` modifies PCI registers for TCSEL and snoop settings, then `azx_init_chip` is called. But `azx_init_chip` performs a controller reset only when `full_reset=1` is passed. The reset logic in `azx_reset` skips the full reset if that flag isn't set, which could leave the CORB/RIRB in an inconsistent state if the controller wasn't properly reset between suspend and resume cycles.\n\nThe critical issue is whether `chip->initialized` gets cleared during suspend—if it remains set to 1, then `azx_init_chip` will return early at line 1211-1212 without actually reinitializing the CORB/RIRB or clearing interrupts.
